<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_military_writers" title="List of military writers">Writers</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:War" title="Template:War"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:War" title="Template talk:War"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:War&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Terrorism</b>, in its broadest sense, is the use of intentional violence and fear to achieve political aims. The term is used in this regard primarily to refer to intentional violence during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peacetime" title="Peacetime">peacetime</a> or in the context of <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a> against <a href="/wiki/Non-combatant" title="Non-combatant">non-combatants</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutral</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_personnel" title="Military personnel">military personnel</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The terms "terrorist" and "terrorism" originated during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> of the late 18th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford-2">[2]</a></sup> but became widely used internationally and gained worldwide attention in the 1970s during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_conflict" title="Northern Ireland conflict">Northern Ireland conflict</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Basque_conflict" title="Basque conflict">Basque conflict</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>. The increased use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_attacks" title="Suicide attacks">suicide attacks</a> from the 1980s onwards was typified by the 2001 <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in the United States.
</p><p>There are various different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definitions_of_terrorism" title="Definitions of terrorism">definitions of terrorism</a>, with no universal agreement about it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCode_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCode-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walzer_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walzer-4">[4]</a></sup> Terrorism is a <a href="/wiki/Loaded_language" title="Loaded language">charged term</a>. It is often used with the connotation of something that is "morally wrong". Governments and non-state groups use the term to abuse or denounce opposing groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walzer_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Walzer-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinclair_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sinclair-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JR.White_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-JR.White-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heryant_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heryant-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruthven_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ruthven-8">[8]</a></sup> Varied political organizations have been accused of using terrorism to achieve their objectives. These include <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_terrorism" title="Left-wing terrorism">left-wing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_terrorism" title="Right-wing terrorism">right-wing</a> political organizations, <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_terrorism" title="Nationalist terrorism">nationalist groups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religious_terrorism" title="Religious terrorism">religious groups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_terror" title="Revolutionary terror">revolutionaries</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">ruling governments</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anti-terrorism_legislation" title="Anti-terrorism legislation">Legislation declaring terrorism a crime</a> has been adopted in many states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-10">[10]</a></sup> When terrorism is perpetrated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation_states" title="Nation states">nation states</a>, it is not considered terrorism by the state conducting it, making legality a largely grey-area issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teichman_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-teichman-11">[11]</a></sup> There is no consensus as to whether terrorism should be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Terrorism_Database" title="Global Terrorism Database">Global Terrorism Database</a>, maintained by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland, College Park</a>, has recorded more than 61,000 incidents of non-state terrorism, resulting in at least 140,000 deaths, between 2000 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>Etymologically, the word terror is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> verb <i>Tersere</i>, which later becomes <i>Terrere</i>. The latter form appears in European languages as early as the 12th century; its first known use in French is the word <i>terrible</i> in 1160. By 1356 the word <i>terreur</i> is in use. <i>Terreur</i> is the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a> term <i>terrour</i>, which later becomes the modern word "terror".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jf_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-jf-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_background">Historical background</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">Reign of Terror</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JacobinVignette03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="239" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/JacobinVignette03.jpg/130px-JacobinVignette03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/JacobinVignette03.jpg/195px-JacobinVignette03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/JacobinVignette03.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JacobinVignette03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seal of the <a href="/wiki/Jacobin" title="Jacobin">Jacobin</a> Club: 'Society of the Jacobins, Friends of Freedom and Equality'</div></div></div>
<p>The term <i>terroriste</i>, meaning "terrorist", is first used in 1794 by the French philosopher <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-No%C3%ABl_Babeuf" title="François-Noël Babeuf">François-Noël Babeuf</a>, who denounces <a href="/wiki/Maximilien_Robespierre" title="Maximilien Robespierre">Maximilien Robespierre</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Jacobin" title="Jacobin">Jacobin</a> regime as a dictatorship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kellner_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-kellner-16">[16]</a></sup> In the years leading up to what became known as the Reign of Terror, the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Manifesto" title="Brunswick Manifesto">Brunswick Manifesto</a> threatened Paris with an "exemplary, never to be forgotten vengeance: the city would be subjected to military punishment and total destruction" if the royal family was harmed, but this only increased the Revolution's will to abolish the monarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-duncan_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-duncan-17">[17]</a></sup> Some writers attitudes about <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> grew less favorable after the French monarchy was abolished in 1792. During the <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">Reign of Terror</a>, which began in July 1793 and lasted thirteen months, Paris was governed by the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Public_Safety" title="Committee of Public Safety">Committee of Public Safety</a> who oversaw a regime of mass executions and public purges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to the French Revolution, ancient philosophers wrote about <a href="/wiki/Tyrannicide" title="Tyrannicide">tyrannicide</a>, as tyranny was seen as the greatest political threat to Greco-Roman civilization. <a href="/wiki/Medieval_philosophy" title="Medieval philosophy">Medieval philosophers</a> were similarly occupied with the concept of tyranny, though the analysis of some theologians like <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> drew a distinction between usurpers, who could be killed by anyone, and legitimate rulers who abused their power—the latter, in Aquinas' view, could only be punished by a public authority. <a href="/wiki/John_of_Salisbury" title="John of Salisbury">John of Salisbury</a> was the first medieval Christian scholar to defend tyrannicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jf_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-jf-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="875" data-file-width="1418" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/300px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/450px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/600px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte" title="Napoléon Bonaparte">Napoléon Bonaparte</a> quelling the <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">October 5, 1795 royalist rebellion</a> in Paris, in front of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89glise_Saint-Roch" title="Église Saint-Roch">Église Saint-Roch</a>, Saint-Honoré Street, paving the way for <a href="/wiki/French_Directory#October_1795_royalist_rebellion" title="French Directory">Directory government</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Most scholars today trace the origins of the modern tactic of terrorism to the Jewish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sicarii_Zealots" title="Sicarii Zealots">Sicarii Zealots</a> who attacked Romans and Jews in 1st-century <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>. They follow its development from the Persian <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Assassins" title="Order of Assassins">Order of Assassins</a> through to 19th-century anarchists. The "Reign of Terror" is usually regarded as an issue of etymology. The term terrorism has generally been used to describe violence by non-state actors rather than government violence since the 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_France" title="Anarchism in France">Anarchist Movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-duncan_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-duncan-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1795, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Burke" title="Edmund Burke">Edmund Burke</a> used the word "Terrorists" in a description of the new <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">French government called 'Directory'</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>At length, after a terrible struggle, the [Directory] Troops prevailed over the Citizens ... To secure them further, they have a strong corps of <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregulars</a>, ready armed. Thousands of those Hell-hounds called <b>Terrorists</b>, whom they had shut up in Prison on their last Revolution, as the Satellites of Tyranny, are let loose on the people.(emphasis added)</p></blockquote>
<p>The terms "terrorism" and "terrorist" gained renewed currency in the 1970s as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">Northern Ireland conflict</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Basque_conflict" title="Basque conflict">Basque conflict</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and the operations of groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_Faction" title="Red Army Faction">Red Army Faction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leila_Khaled" title="Leila Khaled">Leila Khaled</a> was described as a terrorist in a 1970 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(magazine)" title="Life (magazine)">Life</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> A number of books on terrorism were published in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The topic came further to the fore after the <a href="/wiki/1983_Beirut_barracks_bombings" title="1983 Beirut barracks bombings">1983 Beirut barracks bombings</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heryant_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heryant-7">[7]</a></sup> and again after the 2001 <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heryant_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Heryant-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gabriel_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gabriel-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campo_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campo-29">[29]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2002_Bali_bombings" title="2002 Bali bombings">2002 Bali bombings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heryant_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Heryant-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_definitions">Modern definitions</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definitions_of_terrorism" title="Definitions of terrorism">Definitions of terrorism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stragedibologna-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg/220px-Stragedibologna-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg/330px-Stragedibologna-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Stragedibologna-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stragedibologna-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bologna_massacre" title="Bologna massacre">Attack</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a> <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Centrale_railway_station" title="Bologna Centrale railway station">railway station</a> on August 2, 1980, by the neo-fascist group <a href="/wiki/Nuclei_Armati_Rivoluzionari" title="Nuclei Armati Rivoluzionari">Nuclei Armati Rivoluzionari</a>. With 85 deaths, it is the deadliest massacre in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Italy_as_a_Republic" title="History of Italy as a Republic">history of Italy as a Republic</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="802" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg/220px-Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg/330px-Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg/440px-Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myyrmannin_r%C3%A4j%C3%A4hdys.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Myyrmanni_bombing" title="Myyrmanni bombing">2002 bomb attack</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Myyrmanni" title="Myyrmanni">Myyrmanni shopping mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Myyrm%C3%A4ki" title="Myyrmäki">Myyrmäki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vantaa" title="Vantaa">Vantaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>. The bombing was especially shocking for Finland and the other <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, where bombings are extremely rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beslan_school_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="503" data-file-width="399" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Beslan_school_2008.jpg/220px-Beslan_school_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Beslan_school_2008.jpg/330px-Beslan_school_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5f/Beslan_school_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beslan_school_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Beslan_school_siege" title="Beslan school siege">Beslan school siege</a> by Chechen rebels on September 1, 2004. It was the deadliest massacre in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">history of Russia</a> in the 21st century.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2006 it was estimated that there were over 109 different definitions of terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arie_W_2006_pp._45-48_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arie_W_2006_pp._45-48-31">[31]</a></sup> American political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Michael_Walzer" title="Michael Walzer">Michael Walzer</a> in 2002 wrote: "Terrorism is the deliberate killing of innocent people, at random, to spread fear through a whole population and force the hand of its political leaders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walzer_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Walzer-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Hoffman" title="Bruce Hoffman">Bruce Hoffman</a>, an American scholar, has noted that it is not only individual agencies within the same governmental apparatus that cannot agree on a single definition of terrorism. Experts and other long-established scholars in the field are equally incapable of reaching a consensus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman200634_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman200634-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/C._A._J._Coady" title="C. A. J. Coady">C. A. J. Coady</a> has written that the question of how to define terrorism is "irresolvable" because "its natural home is in polemical, ideological and propagandist contexts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teichman_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-teichman-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Experts disagree about "whether terrorism is wrong by definition or just wrong as a matter of fact; they disagree about whether terrorism should be defined in terms of its aims, or its methods, or both, or neither; they disagree about whether states can perpetrate terrorism; they even disagree about the importance or otherwise of <i>terror</i> for a definition of <i>terrorism</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teichman_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-teichman-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_terrorism">State terrorism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">State terrorism</a></div>
<p>State terrorism refers to acts of terrorism conducted by a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> against its own citizens or against another state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations">United Nations</span></h3>
<p>In November 2004, a <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> report described terrorism as any act "intended to cause death or serious bodily harm to civilians or non-combatants with the purpose of intimidating a population or compelling a government or an international organization to do or abstain from doing any act".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">international community</a> has been slow to formulate a universally agreed, legally binding definition of this crime. These difficulties arise from the fact that the term "terrorism" is politically and emotionally charged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman199832_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman199832-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In this regard, Angus Martyn, briefing the Australian parliament, stated,
</p>
<blockquote><p>The international community has never succeeded in developing an accepted comprehensive definition of terrorism. During the 1970s and 1980s, the United Nations attempts to define the term floundered mainly due to differences of opinion between various members about the use of violence in the context of conflicts over national liberation and self-determination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martyn_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martyn-37">[37]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>These divergences have made it impossible for the United Nations to conclude a <a href="/wiki/Definition_of_terrorism#UN_Comprehensive_Convention_(1997–present)" title="Definition of terrorism">Comprehensive Convention on International Terrorism</a> that incorporates a single, all-encompassing, legally binding, criminal law definition of terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The international community has adopted a series of <a href="/wiki/Definition_of_terrorism#The_sectoral_approach" title="Definition of terrorism">sectoral conventions</a> that define and criminalize various types of terrorist activities.
</p><p>Since 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> has repeatedly condemned terrorist acts using the following political description of terrorism:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Criminal acts intended or calculated to provoke a state of terror in the public, a group of persons or particular persons for political purposes are in any circumstance unjustifiable, whatever the considerations of a political, philosophical, ideological, racial, ethnic, religious or any other nature that may be invoked to justify them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._law">U.S. law</span></h3>
<p>Various legal systems and government agencies use different <a href="/wiki/Anti-terrorism_legislation" title="Anti-terrorism legislation">definitions of terrorism in their national legislation</a>.
</p><p>U.S. Code Title 22 Chapter 38, Section 2656f(d) defines terrorism as:
"Premeditated, politically motivated violence perpetrated against noncombatant targets by subnational groups or clandestine agents".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>18 U.S.C. § 2331 defines "international terrorism" and "domestic terrorism" for purposes of Chapter 113B of the Code, entitled "Terrorism":
</p><p>"International terrorism" means activities with the following three characteristics:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Involve violent acts or acts dangerous to human life that violate federal or state law;
</p><p>Appear to be intended (i) to intimidate or coerce a civilian population; (ii) to influence the policy of a government by intimidation or coercion; or (iii) to affect the conduct of a government by mass destruction, assassination, or kidnapping; and
</p><p>
occur primarily outside the territorial jurisdiction of the U.S., or transcend national boundaries in terms of the means by which they are accomplished, the persons they appear intended to intimidate or coerce, or the locale in which their perpetrators operate or seek asylum.</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_spectacle">Media spectacle</span></h3>
<p>A definition proposed by Carsten Bockstette at the <a href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_European_Center_for_Security_Studies" title="George C. Marshall European Center for Security Studies">George C. Marshall European Center for Security Studies</a>, underlines the psychological and tactical aspects of terrorism:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Terrorism is defined as political violence in an asymmetrical conflict that is designed to induce terror and psychic fear (sometimes indiscriminate) through the violent victimization and destruction of noncombatant targets (sometimes iconic symbols). Such acts are meant to send a message from an illicit clandestine organization. The purpose of terrorism is to exploit the media in order to achieve maximum attainable publicity as an amplifying force multiplier in order to influence the targeted audience(s) in order to reach short- and midterm political goals and/or desired long-term end states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bockstette2008_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bockstette2008-42">[42]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Terrorists attack national symbols, which may negatively affect a government, while increasing the prestige of the given <a href="/wiki/List_of_designated_terrorist_groups" title="List of designated terrorist groups">terrorist group</a> or its ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_violence">Political violence</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_violence" title="Political violence">Political violence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luis_Posada_Carriles_-_1963.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="214" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Luis_Posada_Carriles_-_1963.jpg/170px-Luis_Posada_Carriles_-_1963.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/Luis_Posada_Carriles_-_1963.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luis_Posada_Carriles_-_1963.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Luis_Posada_Carriles" title="Luis Posada Carriles">Luis Posada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coordination_of_United_Revolutionary_Organizations" title="Coordination of United Revolutionary Organizations">CORU</a> are widely considered responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Cubana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n_Flight_455" title="Cubana de Aviación Flight 455">1976 bombing of a Cuban airliner</a> that killed 73 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Terrorist acts frequently have a political purpose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janwq32_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janwq32-45">[45]</a></sup> Some official, governmental definitions of terrorism use the criterion of the illegitimacy or unlawfulness of the act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (March 2010)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to distinguish between actions authorized by a government (and thus "lawful") and those of other actors, including individuals and small groups. For example, carrying out a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">strategic bombing</a> on an enemy city, which is designed to affect civilian support for a cause, would not be considered terrorism if it were authorized by a government. This criterion is inherently problematic and is not universally accepted,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Attribution_needed" title="Wikipedia:Attribution needed"><span title="This sentence may contain perspectives and opinions without stating whose they are. (March 2010)">attribution needed</span></a></i>]</sup> because: it denies the existence of <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11jan6yu_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11jan6yu-47">[47]</a></sup> An associated term is <a href="/wiki/Violent_non-state_actor" title="Violent non-state actor">violent non-state actor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11jan4eer_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11jan4eer-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Ali Khan, the distinction lies ultimately in a political judgment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pejorative_use">Pejorative use</span></h2>
<p>Having the connotation of "something morally wrong", the term "terrorism" is often used to abuse or denounce opposite parties, either governments or non-state groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walzer_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Walzer-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinclair_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sinclair-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JR.White_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-JR.White-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heryant_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Heryant-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruthven_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ruthven-8">[8]</a></sup> An example of this is the <i><a href="/wiki/Terruqueo" title="Terruqueo">terruqueo</a></i> political attack used by right-wing groups in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> to target leftist groups or those opposed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo" title="Status quo">status quo</a></i>, likening opponents to guerillas from the <a href="/wiki/Internal_conflict_in_Peru" title="Internal conflict in Peru">internal conflict in Peru</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PROFE1_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-PROFE1-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Those labeled "terrorists" by their opponents rarely identify themselves as such, and typically use other terms or terms specific to their situation, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Separatist" title="Separatist">separatist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_fighter" title="Freedom fighter">freedom fighter</a>, liberator, <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vigilante" title="Vigilante">vigilante</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurgent" title="Insurgent">militant</a>, paramilitary, <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebel</a>, patriot, or any similar-meaning word in other languages and cultures. <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">Jihadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mujahideen" title="Mujahideen">mujahideen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fedayeen" title="Fedayeen">fedayeen</a> are similar Arabic words that have entered the English lexicon. It is common for both parties in a conflict to describe each other as terrorists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janbcvc_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janbcvc-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>On whether particular terrorist acts, such as killing non-combatants, can be justified as the lesser evil in a particular circumstance, philosophers have expressed different views: while, according to David Rodin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utilitarian" title="Utilitarian">utilitarian</a> philosophers can (in theory) conceive of cases in which the evil of terrorism is outweighed by the good that could not be achieved in a less morally costly way, in practice the "harmful effects of undermining the convention of non-combatant immunity is thought to outweigh the goods that may be achieved by particular acts of terrorism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robin_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robin-54">[54]</a></sup> Among the non-utilitarian philosophers, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Walzer" title="Michael Walzer">Michael Walzer</a> argued that terrorism can be morally justified in only one specific case: when "a nation or community faces the extreme threat of complete destruction and the only way it can preserve itself is by intentionally targeting non-combatants,then it is morally entitled to do so".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robin_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robin-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11jannmllk_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11jannmllk-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his book <i>Inside Terrorism</i> <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Hoffman" title="Bruce Hoffman">Bruce Hoffman</a> offered an explanation of why the term <i>terrorism</i> becomes distorted:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>On one point, at least, everyone agrees: <i>terrorism</i> is a pejorative term. It is a word with intrinsically negative connotations that is generally applied to one's enemies and opponents, or to those with whom one disagrees and would otherwise prefer to ignore. 'What is called terrorism,' Brian Jenkins has written, 'thus seems to depend on one's point of view. Use of the term implies a moral judgment; and if one party can successfully attach the label <i>terrorist</i> to its opponent, then it has indirectly persuaded others to adopt its moral viewpoint.' Hence the decision to call someone or label some organization <i>terrorist</i> becomes almost unavoidably subjective, depending largely on whether one sympathizes with or opposes the person/group/cause concerned. If one identifies with the victim of the violence, for example, then the act is terrorism. If, however, one identifies with the perpetrator, the violent act is regarded in a more sympathetic, if not positive (or, at the worst, an ambivalent) light; and it is not terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman199832_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman199832-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>The pejorative connotations of the word can be summed up in the <a href="/wiki/Aphorism" title="Aphorism">aphorism</a>, "One man's terrorist is another man's freedom fighter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janbcvc_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janbcvc-53">[53]</a></sup> This is exemplified when a group using <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregular military</a> methods is an ally of a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a> against a mutual enemy, but later falls out with the state and starts to use those methods against its former ally.
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1911" data-file-width="2707" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/250px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/375px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/500px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Reagan meeting with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afghan_Mujahideen" title="Afghan Mujahideen">Afghan Mujahideen</a> leaders in the Oval Office in 1983</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayan_People%27s_Anti-Japanese_Army" title="Malayan People's Anti-Japanese Army">Malayan People's Anti-Japanese Army</a> were allied with the British, but during the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a>, members of its successor organisation (the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_National_Liberation_Army" title="Malayan National Liberation Army">Malayan National Liberation Army</a>) started campaigns against them, and were branded "terrorists" as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> More recently, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and others in the American administration frequently called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afghan_Mujahideen" title="Afghan Mujahideen">mujaheddin</a> "freedom fighters" during the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> however twenty years later, when a new generation of Afghan men (militant groups like the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> and allies) were fighting against what they perceive to be a regime installed by foreign powers, their attacks were labelled terrorism by <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Groups accused of terrorism understandably prefer terms reflecting legitimate military or ideological action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCCACR_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCCACR-65">[65]</a></sup> Leading terrorism researcher Professor Martin Rudner, director of the Canadian Centre of Intelligence and Security Studies at Ottawa's <a href="/wiki/Carleton_University" title="Carleton University">Carleton University</a>, defines "terrorist acts" as unlawful attacks for political or other ideological goals, and said:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There is the famous statement: 'One man's terrorist is another man's freedom fighter.' But that is grossly misleading. It assesses the validity of the cause when terrorism is an act. One can have a perfectly beautiful cause and yet if one commits terrorist acts, it is terrorism regardless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-famous_quote_one_man's_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-famous_quote_one_man's-66">[66]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Some groups, when involved in a "liberation" struggle, have been called "terrorists" by the Western governments or media. Later, these same persons, as leaders of the liberated nations, are called "statesmen" by similar organizations. Two examples of this phenomenon are the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> laureates <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">Menachem Begin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> editor <a href="/wiki/Julian_Assange" title="Julian Assange">Julian Assange</a> has been called a "terrorist" by <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palin" title="Sarah Palin">Sarah Palin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sometimes, states that are close allies, for reasons of history, culture and politics, can disagree over whether members of a certain organization are terrorists. For instance, some branches of the United States government refused to label members of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a> (IRA) as terrorists while the IRA was using methods against one of the United States' closest allies (the United Kingdom) that the UK branded as terrorism. This was highlighted by the <i>Quinn v. Robinson</i> case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>Media outlets who wish to convey impartiality may limit their usage of "terrorist" and "terrorism" because they are loosely defined, potentially controversial in nature, and subjective terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUSG_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-GUSG-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href='/wiki/2020_Nashville_bombing#Debate_over_"terrorism"_as_a_term' title="2020 Nashville bombing">2020 Nashville bombing revived a debate</a> over the use of the word "terrorism", with critics saying it is quickly applied to attacks by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> but reluctantly if at all used by white <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> men, such as the Nashville bomber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_terrorism" title="History of terrorism">History of terrorism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4052" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png/200px-Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png/300px-Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png/400px-Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fenian_guy_fawkesr1867reduced.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Brotherhood" title="Irish Republican Brotherhood">Irish Republican Brotherhood</a> was one of the earliest organizations to use modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrorist_tactics" title="Terrorist tactics">terrorist tactics</a>. Pictured, "The Fenian <a href="/wiki/Guy_Fawkes" title="Guy Fawkes">Guy Fawkes</a>" by <a href="/wiki/John_Tenniel" title="John Tenniel">John Tenniel</a> (1867).</div></div></div>
<p>Depending on how broadly the term is defined, the roots and practice of terrorism can be traced at least to the 1st century AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofindia.indiatimes.com_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-timesofindia.indiatimes.com-80">[80]</a></sup> According to the contemporary Jewish-Roman historian <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">Josephus</a>, after the Zealotry rebellion against Roman rule in Judea, when some prominent Jewish collaborators with Roman rule were killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman198883_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman198883-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Judas_of_Galilee" title="Judas of Galilee">Judas of Galilee</a> formed a small and more extreme offshoot of the Zealots, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sicarii_Zealots" title="Sicarii Zealots">Sicarii Zealots</a>, in 6 AD. They were a smaller and more radical offshoot of the <a href="/wiki/Zealots" title="Zealots">Zealots</a> which was active in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judaea_Province" title="Judaea Province">Judaea Province</a> at the beginning of the 1st century AD, and they can be considered early terrorists, although this is disputed. Their terror was directed against Jewish "collaborators", including temple priests, <a href="/wiki/Sadducees" title="Sadducees">Sadducees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herodian_dynasty" title="Herodian dynasty">Herodians</a>, and other wealthy elites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman1988167_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman1988167-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term "terrorism" itself was originally used to describe the actions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacobin_Club" title="Jacobin Club">Jacobin Club</a> during the "<a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">Reign of Terror</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. "Terror is nothing other than justice, prompt, severe, inflexible", said Jacobin leader <a href="/wiki/Maximilien_Robespierre" title="Maximilien Robespierre">Maximilien Robespierre</a>. In 1795, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Burke" title="Edmund Burke">Edmund Burke</a> denounced the Jacobins for letting "thousands of those hell-hounds called Terrorists ... loose on the people" of France.
</p><p>In January 1858, Italian patriot <a href="/wiki/Felice_Orsini" title="Felice Orsini">Felice Orsini</a> threw three bombs in an attempt to assassinate French Emperor <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crenshaw38_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crenshaw38-84">[84]</a></sup> Eight bystanders were killed and 142 injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crenshaw38_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crenshaw38-84">[84]</a></sup> The incident played a crucial role as an inspiration for the development of the early terrorist groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crenshaw38_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-Crenshaw38-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>Arguably the first organization to utilize modern terrorist techniques was the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Brotherhood" title="Irish Republican Brotherhood">Irish Republican Brotherhood</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> founded in 1858 as a revolutionary Irish nationalist group<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> that carried out attacks in England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The group initiated the <a href="/wiki/Fenian_dynamite_campaign" title="Fenian dynamite campaign">Fenian dynamite campaign</a> in 1881, one of the first modern terror campaigns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Instead of earlier forms of terrorism based on political assassination, this campaign used timed <a href="/wiki/Explosive" title="Explosive">explosives</a> with the express aim of sowing fear in the very heart of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">metropolitan Britain</a>, in order to achieve political gains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another early terrorist-type group was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narodnaya_Volya_(organization)" title="Narodnaya Volya (organization)">Narodnaya Volya</a>, founded in Russia in 1878 as a revolutionary anarchist group inspired by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Nechayev" title="Sergei Nechayev">Sergei Nechayev</a> and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propaganda_by_the_deed" title="Propaganda by the deed">propaganda by the deed</a>" theorist <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Pisacane" title="Carlo Pisacane">Carlo Pisacane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofindia.indiatimes.com_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-timesofindia.indiatimes.com-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdi.org_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdi.org-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffman19985_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffman19985-91">[91]</a></sup> The group developed ideas—such as <a href="/wiki/Targeted_killing" title="Targeted killing">targeted killing</a> of the 'leaders of oppression'—that were to become the hallmark of subsequent violence by small non-state groups, and they were convinced that the developing technologies of the age—such as the invention of dynamite, which they were the first anarchist group to make widespread use of<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>—enabled them to strike directly and with discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_C._Rapoport" title="David C. Rapoport">David Rapoport</a> refers to four major waves of global terrorism: "the Anarchist, the Anti-Colonial, the New Left, and the Religious. The first three have been completed and lasted around 40 years; the fourth is now in its third decade."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Terrorism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Depending on the country, the political system, and the time in history, the types of terrorism are varying.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terro.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="646" data-file-width="653" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Terro.jpg/250px-Terro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Terro.jpg/375px-Terro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Terro.jpg/500px-Terro.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terro.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Number of failed, foiled or successful terrorist attacks by year and type within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Source: <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europol_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europol-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KD_1946.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="672" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/KD_1946.JPG/250px-KD_1946.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/KD_1946.JPG/375px-KD_1946.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/KD_1946.JPG/500px-KD_1946.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KD_1946.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/King_David_Hotel_bombing" title="King David Hotel bombing">King David Hotel bombing</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zionist" title="Zionist">Zionist</a> militant group <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">Irgun</a>, July 1946</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1860" data-file-width="2810" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg/250px-BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg/375px-BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg/500px-BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BombenanschlagUS-BotschaftBeirut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of damage to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1983_United_States_embassy_bombing" title="1983 United States embassy bombing">U.S. Embassy in the aftermath of the 1983 Beirut bombing</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Organization" title="Islamic Jihad Organization">Islamic Jihad Organization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a></div></div></div>
<p>In early 1975, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Justice" title="National Institute of Justice">Law Enforcement Assistant Administration</a> in the United States formed the National Advisory Committee on Criminal Justice Standards and Goals. One of the five volumes that the committee wrote was titled <i>Disorders and Terrorism</i>, produced by the Task Force on Disorders and Terrorism under the direction of H. H. A. Cooper, Director of the Task Force staff.
</p><p>The Task Force defines terrorism as "a tactic or technique by means of which a violent act or the threat thereof is used for the prime purpose of creating overwhelming fear for coercive purposes". It classified disorders and terrorism into six categories:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Civil disorder</b> – A form of collective violence interfering with the <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a>, security, and normal functioning of the community.</li>
<li><b>Political terrorism</b> – <a href="/wiki/Violence" title="Violence">Violent</a> criminal behaviour designed primarily to generate <a href="/wiki/Fear" title="Fear">fear</a> in the community, or substantial segment of it, for political purposes.</li>
<li><b>Non-Political terrorism</b> – Terrorism that is not aimed at political purposes but which exhibits "conscious design to create and maintain a high degree of fear for <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercive</a> purposes, but the end is individual or collective gain rather than the achievement of a political objective".</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Anonymous_terrorism" title="Anonymous terrorism">Anonymous terrorism</a></b> – In the two decades prior to 2016–19, "fewer than half" of all terrorist attacks were either "claimed by their perpetrators or convincingly attributed by governments to specific terrorist groups". A number of theories have been advanced as to why this has happened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1_February_2019_Economist_why_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-1_February_2019_Economist_why-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Quasi-terrorism</b> – The activities incidental to the commission of crimes of violence that are similar in form and method to genuine terrorism but which nevertheless lack its essential ingredient. It is not the main purpose of the quasi-terrorists to induce terror in the immediate victim as in the case of genuine terrorism, but the quasi-terrorist uses the modalities and techniques of the genuine terrorist and produces similar consequences and reaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> For example, the fleeing <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felon</a> who takes <a href="/wiki/Hostage" title="Hostage">hostages</a> is a quasi-terrorist, whose methods are similar to those of the genuine terrorist but whose purposes are quite different.</li>
<li><b>Limited political terrorism</b> – Genuine political terrorism is characterized by a <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a> approach; limited political terrorism refers to "acts of terrorism which are committed for <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">ideological</a> or political motives but which are not part of a concerted campaign to capture control of the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a>".</li>
<li><b>Official or state terrorism</b> – "referring to nations whose rule is based upon <a href="/wiki/Fear" title="Fear">fear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">oppression</a> that reach similar to terrorism or such proportions". It may be referred to as <b>Structural Terrorism</b> defined broadly as terrorist acts carried out by governments in pursuit of political objectives, often as part of their foreign policy.</li></ul>
<p>Other sources have defined the typology of terrorism in different ways, for example, broadly classifying it into <b>domestic terrorism</b> and <b>international terrorism</b>, or using categories such as vigilante terrorism or insurgent terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> One way the typology of terrorism may be defined:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Political terrorism</b>
<ul><li><b>Sub-state terrorism</b>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_terrorism" title="Revolutionary terrorism">Social revolutionary terrorism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nationalist_terrorism" title="Nationalist terrorism">Nationalist-separatist terrorism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Religious_terrorism" title="Religious terrorism">Religious extremist terrorism</a>
<ul><li>Religious fundamentalist Terrorism</li>
<li>New religions terrorism</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Right-wing_terrorism" title="Right-wing terrorism">Right-wing terrorism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Left-wing_terrorism" title="Left-wing terrorism">Left-wing terrorism</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Communist_terrorism" title="Communist terrorism">Communist terrorism</a></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/State-sponsored_terrorism" title="State-sponsored terrorism">State-sponsored terrorism</a></b></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">Regime or state terrorism</a></b></li></ul></li>
<li><b>Criminal terrorism</b></li>
<li><b>Pathological terrorism</b></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes_and_motivations">Causes and motivations</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Choice_of_terrorism_as_a_tactic">Choice of terrorism as a tactic</span></h3>
<p>Individuals and groups choose terrorism as a tactic because it can:
</p>
<ul><li>Act as a form of <a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_warfare" title="Asymmetric warfare">asymmetric warfare</a> in order to directly force a government to agree to demands</li>
<li>Intimidate a group of people into capitulating to the demands in order to avoid future injury</li>
<li>Get attention and thus political support for a cause</li>
<li>Directly inspire more people to the cause (such as revolutionary acts) – <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_of_the_deed" title="Propaganda of the deed">propaganda of the deed</a></li>
<li>Indirectly inspire more people to the cause by provoking a hostile response or over-reaction from enemies to the cause<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Think_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Think-106">[106]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Attacks on "collaborators" are used to intimidate people from cooperating with the state in order to undermine state control. This strategy was used in Ireland, in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> during their independence struggles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>Stated <a href="/wiki/Motives_for_the_September_11_attacks" title="Motives for the September 11 attacks">motives for the September 11 attacks</a> included inspiring more fighters to join the cause of repelling the United States from Muslim countries with a successful high-profile attack. The attacks prompted some criticism from domestic and international observers regarding perceived injustices in U.S. foreign policy that provoked the attacks, but the larger practical effect was that the United States government declared a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a> that resulted in substantial military engagements in several Muslim-majority countries. Various commentators have inferred that <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> expected a military response, and welcomed it as a provocation that would result in more Muslims fight the United States. Some commentators believe that the resulting anger and suspicion directed toward innocent Muslims living in Western countries and the indignities inflicted upon them by security forces and the general public also contributes to radicalization of new recruits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Think_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-Think-106">[106]</a></sup> Despite criticism that the Iraqi government had no involvement with the September 11 attacks, Bush declared the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a> to be part of the War on Terror. The resulting backlash and instability enabled the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> and the temporary creation of an Islamic caliphate holding territory in Iraq and Syria, until ISIL lost its territory through military defeats.
</p><p>Attacks used to draw international attention to struggles that are otherwise unreported have included the <a href="/wiki/Dawson%27s_Field_hijackings" title="Dawson's Field hijackings">Palestinian airplane hijackings in 1970</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1975_Dutch_train_hostage_crisis" title="1975 Dutch train hostage crisis">1975 Dutch train hostage crisis</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes_motivating_terrorism">Causes motivating terrorism</span></h3>
<p>Specific political or social causes have included:
</p>
<ul><li>Independence or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Separatist" title="Separatist">separatist</a> movements</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irredentist" title="Irredentist">Irredentist</a> movements</li>
<li>Adoption of a particular political philosophy, such as <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Left-wing_terrorism" title="Left-wing terrorism">left-wing terrorism</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a> (possibly through a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coup" title="Coup">coup</a> or as an ideology of an independence or separatist movement)</li>
<li>Environmental protection (<a href="/wiki/Eco-terrorism" title="Eco-terrorism">eco-terrorism</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Supremacism" title="Supremacism">Supremacism</a> of a particular group
<ul><li>Preventing a rival group from sharing or occupying a particular territory (such as by discouraging immigration or encouraging flight)</li>
<li>Subjugation of a particular population (such as <a href="/wiki/Lynching_in_the_United_States" title="Lynching in the United States">lynching of African Americans</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li>Spread or dominance of a particular religion – <a href="/wiki/Religious_terrorism" title="Religious terrorism">religious terrorism</a></li>
<li>Ending perceived government <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">oppression</a></li>
<li>Responding to a violent act (for example, tit-for-tat attacks in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>, in <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a> in Northern Ireland, or <a href="/wiki/Timothy_McVeigh" title="Timothy McVeigh">Timothy McVeigh</a>'s revenge for the <a href="/wiki/Waco_siege" title="Waco siege">Waco siege</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruby_Ridge" title="Ruby Ridge">Ruby Ridge</a> incident)</li></ul>
<p>Causes for <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_terrorism" title="Right-wing terrorism">right-wing terrorism</a> have included <a href="/wiki/White_nationalism" title="White nationalism">white nationalism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnonationalism" title="Ethnonationalism">ethnonationalism</a>, fascism, anti-socialism, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-abortion_movement" title="Anti-abortion movement">anti-abortion movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tax_resistance" title="Tax resistance">tax resistance</a>.
</p><p>Sometimes terrorists on the same side fight for different reasons. For example, in the <a href="/wiki/Chechen%E2%80%93Russian_conflict" title="Chechen–Russian conflict">Chechen–Russian conflict</a> secular Chechens using terrorist tactics fighting for national independence are allied with radical Islamist terrorists who have arrived from other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_and_social_factors">Personal and social factors</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Radicalization" title="Radicalization">Radicalization</a></div>
<p>Various personal and social factors may influence the personal choice of whether to join a terrorist group or attempt an act of terror, including:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Identity_(social_science)" title="Identity (social science)">Identity</a>, including affiliation with a particular culture, ethnicity, or religion</li>
<li>Previous exposure to violence</li>
<li>Financial reward (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority_Martyrs_Fund" title="Palestinian Authority Martyrs Fund">Palestinian Authority Martyrs Fund</a>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_health_disorder" title="Mental health disorder">Mental health disorder</a></li>
<li>Social isolation</li>
<li>Perception that the cause responds to a profound injustice or indignity</li></ul>
<p>A report conducted by Paul Gill, John Horgan and Paige Deckert<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (October 2019)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Terrorism#Dubious" title="Talk:Terrorism">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> found that for "lone wolf" terrorists:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>43% were motivated by religious beliefs</li>
<li>32% had pre-existing mental health disorders, while many more are found to have mental health problems upon arrest</li>
<li>At least 37% lived alone at the time of their event planning and/or execution, a further 26% lived with others, and no data were available for the remaining cases</li>
<li>40% were unemployed at the time of their arrest or terrorist event</li>
<li>19% subjectively experienced being disrespected by others</li>
<li>14% percent experienced being the victim of verbal or physical assault</li></ul>
<p>Ariel Merari, a psychologist who has studied the psychological profiles of suicide terrorists since 1983 through media reports that contained biographical details, interviews with the suicides' families, and interviews with jailed would-be <a href="/wiki/Suicide_attack" title="Suicide attack">suicide attackers</a>, concluded that they were unlikely to be psychologically abnormal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In comparison to economic theories of criminal behaviour, Scott Atran found that suicide terrorists exhibit none of the socially dysfunctional attributes—such as fatherless, friendless, jobless situations—or suicidal symptoms. By which he means, they do not kill themselves simply out of hopelessness or a sense of 'having nothing to lose'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>Abrahm suggests that terrorist organizations do not select terrorism for its political effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abrahm_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abrahm-112">[112]</a></sup> Individual terrorists tend to be motivated more by a desire for social solidarity with other members of their organization than by political platforms or strategic objectives, which are often murky and undefined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abrahm_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-Abrahm-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>Michael Mousseau shows possible relationships between the type of economy within a country and ideology associated with terrorism.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AUDIENCE" title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE"><span title="An editor has requested that an example be provided. (October 2019)"><span style="font-style:italic; padding-right:0.15em;">example  needed</span></span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Many terrorists have a history of domestic violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Democracy_and_domestic_terrorism">Democracy and domestic terrorism</span></h2>
<p>Terrorism is most common in nations with intermediate political freedom, and it is least common in the most democratic nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some examples of "terrorism" in non-democratic nations include <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> in Spain under <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> (although the group's terrorist activities increased sharply after Franco's death),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janfjlk_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janfjlk-119">[119]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists</a> in pre-war <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Shining_Path" title="Shining Path">Shining Path</a> in Peru under <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fujimori" title="Alberto Fujimori">Alberto Fujimori</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janaawsw_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janaawsw-121">[121]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers Party">Kurdistan Workers Party</a> when <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> was ruled by military leaders and the <a href="/wiki/African_National_Congress" title="African National Congress">ANC</a> in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11jangvdf_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11jangvdf-122">[122]</a></sup> Democracies, such as Japan, the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, have experienced domestic terrorism.
</p><p>While a democratic nation espousing <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a> may claim a sense of higher moral ground than other regimes, an act of terrorism within such a state may cause a dilemma: whether to maintain its civil liberties and thus risk being perceived as ineffective in dealing with the problem; or alternatively to restrict its civil liberties and thus risk delegitimizing its claim of supporting civil liberties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws11janetrr_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws11janetrr-123">[123]</a></sup> For this reason, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homegrown_terrorism" title="Homegrown terrorism">homegrown terrorism</a> has started to be seen as a greater threat, as stated by former CIA Director Michael Hayden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayden_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hayden-124">[124]</a></sup> This dilemma, some social theorists would conclude, may very well play into the initial plans of the acting terrorist(s); namely, to delegitimize the state and cause a systematic shift towards anarchy via the accumulation of negative sentiments towards the state system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_terrorism">Religious terrorism</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_terrorism" title="Religious terrorism">Religious terrorism</a></div>
